href="#cite_note-VideoGamer-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Dota 2</i> received "universal acclaim" according to <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Metacritic_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and has been listed by multiple publications as one of the <a href="/wiki/Greatest_video_games_of_all_time" class="mw-redirect" title="Greatest video games of all time">greatest video games of all time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GI2018_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GI2018-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In a preview of the game in 2012, Rich McCormick of <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Gamer" title="PC Gamer">PC Gamer</a></i> thought that <i>Dota 2</i> was "an unbelievably deep and complex game that offers the purest sequel to the original <i>Defense of the Ancients</i>. Rewarding like few others, but tough".<sup id="cite_ref-PCG_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCG-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Adam Biessener, the editor who authored the announcement article for <i>Dota 2</i> for <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i> in 2010, praised Valve for maintaining the same mechanics and game balance that made <i>Defense of the Ancients</i> successful nearly a decade prior<sup id="cite_ref-GIReview_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GIReview-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and Quintin Smith of <a href="/wiki/Eurogamer" title="Eurogamer">Eurogamer</a> described <i>Dota 2</i> as the "supreme form of the MOBA which everyone else working in the genre is trying to capture like lightning in a bottle".<sup id="cite_ref-EuroGReview_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EuroGReview-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The most frequently praised aspects of the game were its depth, delivery, and overall balance. Chris Thursten of <i>PC Gamer</i> described the gameplay as being "deep and rewarding".<sup id="cite_ref-PCGUS_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGUS-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Martin Gaston of <i><a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a></i> complimented Valve for the artistic design and delivery of <i>Dota 2</i>, citing the execution of the user interface design, voice acting, and characterization as exceeding those of the game's competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-GSpot_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Phill Cameron of <i><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a></i> and James Kozanitis of <i><a href="/wiki/Hardcore_Gamer" title="Hardcore Gamer">Hardcore Gamer</a></i> both praised <i>Dota 2</i> for its <a href="/wiki/Free-to-play" title="Free-to-play">free-to-play</a> business model that was not affected by cosmetic items, with Kozanitis stating that <i>Dota 2</i> was "the only game to do free-to-play right".<sup id="cite_ref-IGNReview_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNReview-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Nick Kolan of <i>IGN</i> also agreed, comparing the game's business model to Valve's <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i>, which uses a nearly identical system.<sup id="cite_ref-LoL_vs_Dota_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoL_vs_Dota-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Post-release additions to the game were also praised, such as the addition of <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">virtual reality</a> (VR) support in 2016. Ben Kuchera of <i>Polygon</i> thought that spectating games in VR was "amazing", comparing it to being able to watch an <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> game on television with the ability to jump onto the field at any time to see the <a href="/wiki/Quarterback" title="Quarterback">quarterback</a>'s point of view.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Chris Thursten of <i>PC Gamer</i> agreed, calling the experience "incredible" and unlike any other esports spectating system that existed prior to it.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Sam Machkovech of <i>Ars Technica</i> also praised the addition, believing that the functionality could "attract serious attention from gamers and non-gamers alike".<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the majority of reviewers gave <i>Dota 2</i> highly positive reviews, a common criticism was that the game maintains a steep learning curve that requires exceptional commitment to overcome. While providing a moderately positive review that praised Valve's product stability, Fredrik Åslund from the Swedish division of <i><a href="/wiki/Gamereactor" title="Gamereactor">Gamereactor</a></i> described his first match of <i>Dota 2</i> as one of the most humiliating and inhospitable experiences of his gaming career, citing the learning curve and players' attitudes as unwelcoming.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Benjamin Danneberg of <i><a href="/wiki/GameStar" title="GameStar">GameStar</a></i> alluded to the learning curve as a "learning cliff", calling the newcomer's experience to be painful, with the tutorial feature new to the <i>Dota</i> franchise only being partially successful.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In a review for the <i><a href="/wiki/Metro_(British_newspaper)" title="Metro (British newspaper)">Metro</a></i> newspaper, <i>Dota 2</i> was criticized for not compensating for the flaws with the learning curve from <i>Defense of the Ancients</i>, as well as the sometimes hostile community, which is commonly criticized in multiplayer online battle arena games.<sup id="cite_ref-Metro_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metro-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Peter Bright of <i><a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a></i> also directed criticism at the ability for third-party websites to allow <a href="/wiki/Skin_gambling" title="Skin gambling">skin gambling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sports_betting" title="Sports betting">betting</a> on match results, similar to <a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Global_Offensive#Gambling_and_third-party_betting" title="Counter-Strike: Global Offensive">controversies that also existed</a> with Valve's <i><a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Global_Offensive" title="Counter-Strike: Global Offensive">Counter-Strike: Global Offensive</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gambling_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gambling-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Using <i>Dota 2</i> as an example, Bright thought that Valve had built gambling elements directly into their games, and had issues with the unregulated practice, which he said was often used by underage players and regions where <a href="/wiki/Gaming_law" title="Gaming law">gambling is illegal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gambling_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gambling-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Australian senator <a href="/wiki/Nick_Xenophon" title="Nick Xenophon">Nick Xenophon</a> had similar sentiment, stating that he wanted to introduce legislation in his country to minimize underage access to gambling within video games, including <i>Dota 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> In response to the controversy, Valve and <i>Dota 2</i> project manager, Erik Johnson, stated that they would be taking action against the third-party sites, saying that the practice was not allowed by their <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">API</a> or their user agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Comparisons of <i>Dota 2</i> to other MOBA games are commonplace, with the game's mechanics and business model often being directly compared with <i><a href="/wiki/League_of_Legends" title="League of Legends">League of Legends</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Heroes_of_the_Storm" title="Heroes of the Storm">Heroes of the Storm</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-LoL_vs_Dota_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoL_vs_Dota-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Contrasting it with <i>League of Legends</i>, T.J. Hafer of PC Gamer called <i>Dota 2</i> the "superior experience", stating that he thought the game was "all about counterplay", with most of the heroes being designed to directly counter another.<sup id="cite_ref-Face_Off_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Face_Off-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Hafer also preferred the way the game handled its hero selection pool, with all of them being unlocked right from the start, unlike in <i>League of Legends</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Face_Off_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Face_Off-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Comparing <i>Dota 2</i> to <i>Heroes of the Storm</i>, Jason Parker of <a href="/wiki/CNET" title="CNET">CNET</a> said that while <i>Heroes of the Storm</i> was easier to get into, the complexities and depth of <i>Dota 2</i> would be appreciated more by those who put in the time to master it.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Further comparing it to <i><a href="/wiki/Heroes_of_Newerth" title="Heroes of Newerth">Heroes of Newerth</a></i>, players from the professional <i>Dota 2</i> team <a href="/wiki/OG_(esports)" title="OG (esports)">OG</a> said that most <i>Heroes of Newerth</i> players were able to transition over easily to the game, due to the strong similarities that both games share.<sup id="cite_ref-HoN_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoN-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</span></h3>
<p>Following its first public showing in 2011, <i>Dota 2</i> won <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a>'s People's Choice Award.<sup id="cite_ref-IGNAward_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNAward-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Gamer" title="PC Gamer">PC Gamer</a></i> listed <i>Dota 2</i> as a nominee for their <a href="/wiki/Game_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Game of the Year">Game of the Year</a> award, as well as the best esports title of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, <i>Dota 2</i> won the esport game of the year award from <i>PC Gamer</i><sup id="cite_ref-PCE-Sport2013_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCE-Sport2013-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/OnGamers" title="OnGamers">onGamers</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-onGamersESport2013_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onGamersESport2013-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GameTrailers" title="GameTrailers">GameTrailers</a> also awarded the game the award for Best PC Game of 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-GTBestPCGame_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GTBestPCGame-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> with IGN also awarding it the Best PC Strategy &amp; Tactics Game, Best PC Multiplayer Game, and People's Choice Award.<sup id="cite_ref-IGNBestStrategyTactics_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNBestStrategyTactics-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IGNBestMultiplayer_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNBestMultiplayer-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, <i>Game Informer</i> recognized <i>Dota 2</i> for the categories of Best PC Exclusive, Best Competitive Multiplayer and Best Strategy of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-GIBestof2013_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GIBestof2013-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The same year, <i>Dota 2</i> was nominated for a number of Game of the Year awards by <i><a href="/wiki/Destructoid" title="Destructoid">Destructoid</a></i>, including the award for the best competitive game. While the staff selected <i><a href="/wiki/StarCraft_II:_Heart_of_the_Swarm" title="StarCraft II: Heart of the Swarm">StarCraft II: Heart of the Swarm</a></i>, <i>Dota 2</i> received the majority of the votes distributed between the nine nominees.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dota 2</i> was later nominated for the best multiplayer game at the <a href="/wiki/10th_British_Academy_Games_Awards" title="10th British Academy Games Awards">10th British Academy Games Awards</a> in 2014, but lost to <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_V" title="Grand Theft Auto V">Grand Theft Auto V</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> and was nominated for esports Game of the Year at <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards" title="The Game Awards">The Game Awards</a> at its 2015, 2016, and 2017 events,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> while winning the award for best MOBA at the 2015 Global Game Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The game was also nominated for the community created "Love/Hate Relationship" award at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Steam_Awards" title="Steam Awards">Steam Awards</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Through 2017–2018, the game was nominated for Choice Video Game at the <a href="/wiki/2017_Teen_Choice_Awards" title="2017 Teen Choice Awards">2017 Teen Choice Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> for esports Game of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Joystick_Awards" title="Golden Joystick Awards">Golden Joystick Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Video_Game_Trade_Reviewers" title="National Academy of Video Game Trade Reviewers">National Academy of Video Game Trade Reviewers</a> Awards,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> and as <i>IGN</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> best spectator game.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg/190px-Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg" width="190" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg/285px-Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg/380px-Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dota_2_Juggernaut_cosplay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A fan <a href="/wiki/Cosplay" title="Cosplay">cosplaying</a> as Juggernaut, one of the game's 116 playable characters</div></div></div>
<p>Two months before its official release, <i>Dota 2</i> broke the all-time Steam record for most <a href="/wiki/Concurrent_players" class="mw-redirect" title="Concurrent players">concurrent players</a> with nearly 330,000.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Simultaneous with this benchmark, the concurrent number of <i>Dota 2</i> players in May 2013 outweighed the number of players for the rest of Steam's top ten most-played games combined.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dota 2</i> was the first game in Steam's history to have over a million concurrent players,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> and remained as the most played game by concurrent players on the platform for four years,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> never dropping below first place for any extended period of time until being surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/PlayerUnknown%27s_Battlegrounds" title="PlayerUnknown&#39;s Battlegrounds">PlayerUnknown's Battlegrounds</a></i> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Viewership and followings of professional <i>Dota 2</i> leagues and tournaments are also popular, with peak viewership numbers of some events reaching upwards in the millions.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Some Asian schools and universities, such as the <a href="/wiki/Asia_Pacific_University_of_Technology_%26_Innovation" title="Asia Pacific University of Technology &amp; Innovation">Asia Pacific University of Technology &amp; Innovation</a> in Malaysia, have held courses on <i>Dota 2</i>, teaching students the fundamentals and core skills to use during the game.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dota 2</i> has also been a part of traditional <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport events</a>, such as under the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_sports_at_the_2017_Asian_Indoor_and_Martial_Arts_Games" title="Electronic sports at the 2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games">esports category</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2017_Asian_Indoor_and_Martial_Arts_Games" title="2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games">2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Promotional <a href="/wiki/Tie-in" title="Tie-in">tie-ins</a> to other video games and media have been added to <i>Dota 2</i> since release, including custom <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2" title="Half-Life 2">Half-Life 2</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Announcer_packs_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Announcer_packs-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Bastion_(video_game)" title="Bastion (video game)">Bastion</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Announcer_packs_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Announcer_packs-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Portal_(video_game_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Portal (video game series)">Portal</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Stanley_Parable" title="The Stanley Parable">The Stanley Parable</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rick_and_Morty" title="Rick and Morty">Rick and Morty</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Fallout_4" title="Fallout 4">Fallout 4</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Deus_Ex:_Mankind_Divided" title="Deus Ex: Mankind Divided">Deus Ex: Mankind Divided</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Darkest_Dungeon" title="Darkest Dungeon">Darkest Dungeon</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> announcer packs, which replace the game's default announcer with ones based on those franchises. In addition to announcer packs, well-known musical artists have written music packs that can replace the game's default soundtrack, such as <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Deadmau5" title="Deadmau5">deadmau5</a> and Singaporean songwriter <a href="/wiki/JJ_Lin" title="JJ Lin">JJ Lin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> To coincide with the Windows release of <a href="/wiki/Square_Enix" title="Square Enix">Square Enix</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_Type-0_HD" title="Final Fantasy Type-0 HD">Final Fantasy Type-0 HD</a></i> in August 2015, a bundle containing a custom loading screen, a <a href="/wiki/Moogle" class="mw-redirect" title="Moogle">Moogle</a> ward, and a <a href="/wiki/Chocobo" title="Chocobo">Chocobo</a> courier were added the same month.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> In April 2016, Valve announced a cross-promotional workshop contest for <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Total_War:_Warhammer" title="Total War: Warhammer">Total War: Warhammer</a></i>, with the winning entries being included in the game later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, a cosmetic set based on the <a href="/wiki/Companion_Cube" class="mw-redirect" title="Companion Cube">Companion Cube</a> from the <i>Portal</i> series was released as part of <a href="/wiki/The_International_2017" title="The International 2017">that year's</a> International compendium for the hero known as "Io".<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> In December of the same year, the character <a href="/wiki/Amaterasu_(%C5%8Ckami)" title="Amaterasu (Ōkami)">Amaterasu</a> from <a href="/wiki/Capcom" title="Capcom">Capcom</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%8Ckami" title="Ōkami">Ōkami</a></i> was included as a courier for those who had pre-ordered the PC release of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The popularity of <i>Dota 2</i> led Valve to produce apparel, accessories, <a href="/wiki/Poster" title="Poster">posters</a>, and a number of other products featuring the heroes and other elements from the game. In addition, Valve secured licensing contracts with third-party producers; the first of these deals concerned a <i>Dota 2</i> themed <a href="/wiki/SteelSeries" title="SteelSeries">SteelSeries</a> <a href="/wiki/Mousepad" title="Mousepad">mousepad</a>, which was announced at Gamescom 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Theatrical_property" title="Theatrical property">prop</a> studio that creates the "Aegis of Champions" trophy for winners of The International,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> announced a product line that would include statues, weapons, and armor based on <i>Dota 2</i> characters and items.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> In February 2013, the <a href="/wiki/National_Entertainment_Collectibles_Association" title="National Entertainment Collectibles Association">National Entertainment Collectibles Association</a> announced a new toy line featuring hero-themed action figures at the <a href="/wiki/American_International_Toy_Fair" title="American International Toy Fair">American International Toy Fair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> At Gamescom 2015, an <a href="/wiki/HTC_Vive" title="HTC Vive">HTC Vive</a> <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">virtual reality</a> (VR) <a href="/wiki/Tech_demo" class="mw-redirect" title="Tech demo">tech demo</a> based around the shopkeeper of the game's item shop was showcased, allowing participants to interact with various items and objects from the game in VR.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> The demo, known as <i>Secret Shop</i>, was later included the following year on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lab_(video_game)" title="The Lab (video game)">The Lab</a></i>, Valve's virtual reality compilation game.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> After the conclusion of The International 2015, Valve awarded the Collector's Aegis of Champions, which was a 1/5th scale <a href="/wiki/Brass" title="Brass">brass</a> replica of the Aegis of Champions trophy, to those with compendiums of 1,000 levels or more.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Valve awarded the Collector's Aegis again the following year for The International 2016, as well as selling a limited edition <i>Dota 2</i> themed HTC Vive <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality_headset" title="Virtual reality headset">virtual reality headset</a> during the event.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, an 18-track official soundtrack was released by <a href="/wiki/Ipecac_Recordings" title="Ipecac Recordings">Ipecac Recordings</a>, including a version on vinyl.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Digital_collectible_card_game" title="Digital collectible card game">digital collectible card game</a> by Valve, titled <i>Artifact</i>, was released for PC-platforms in November 2018, and is planned for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> devices the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> It was designed by <i><a href="/wiki/Magic:_The_Gathering" title="Magic: The Gathering">Magic: The Gathering</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Richard_Garfield" title="Richard Garfield">Richard Garfield</a>, and is developed alongside <i>Dota 2</i>, introducing new heroes and other content for both games in tandem.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg/250px-Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg" width="250" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg/375px-Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg/500px-Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1806" data-file-height="1344" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dota_2_vanguard_prop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Physical props, based on <a href="/wiki/Item_(gaming)" title="Item (gaming)">items</a> from the game, being sold as merchandise at The International 2012</div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Documentary" class="mw-redirect" title="Documentary">documentary</a> on the game and its professional scene was produced by Valve and released in March 2014. Known as <i><a href="/wiki/Free_to_Play_(film)" title="Free to Play (film)">Free to Play</a></i>, the film follows three players during their time at the first International in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> American <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> player <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Lin" title="Jeremy Lin">Jeremy Lin</a>, who was a <a href="/wiki/Linsanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Linsanity">media sensation at the time</a>, had a guest appearance in the film, where he called the game "a way of life".<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Lin later compared the game and the professional gaming scene in general to basketball and other traditional sporting events, saying that there was not much of a difference between the two,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> while also comparing various <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> <a href="/wiki/All-star" title="All-star">all-stars</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Curry" title="Stephen Curry">Stephen Curry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kobe_Bryant" title="Kobe Bryant">Kobe Bryant</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LeBron_James" title="LeBron James">LeBron James</a>, to different heroes in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> <span id="True_Sight"></span>Starting in 2016, Valve began producing an episodic documentary series titled <i>True Sight</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_successor" title="Spiritual successor">spiritual successor</a> to <i>Free to Play</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-True_Sight_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-True_Sight-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The first three episodes followed the professional teams <a href="/wiki/Evil_Geniuses" title="Evil Geniuses">Evil Geniuses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fnatic" title="Fnatic">Fnatic</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Major" title="Boston Major">Boston Major</a> tournament in late 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-True_Sight_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-True_Sight-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Three more episodes were released over the next two years, focusing on the grand finals of the <a href="/wiki/Kiev_Major" title="Kiev Major">Kiev Major</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_International_2017" title="The International 2017">The International 2017</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_International_2018" title="The International 2018">The International 2018</a> tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Valve have also officially endorsed <a href="/wiki/Cosplay" title="Cosplay">cosplay</a> competitions featuring the game's heroes, which take place during downtime at professional <i>Dota 2</i> tournaments and feature prize pools of their own.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Creation of <i>Dota 2</i>-themed <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">CGI videos</a>, mostly created by the community with <a href="/wiki/Source_Filmmaker" title="Source Filmmaker">Source Filmmaker</a>, also take place.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Similar to the cosplay competitions, Valve holds short film contests every year at The International, with winners of the competition also being awarded prize money.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Valve have created free <a href="/wiki/Webcomic" title="Webcomic">webcomics</a> featuring some of the heroes, further detailing their background lore.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> A physical collection of the comics was released as <i>Dota 2: The Comic Collection</i> by <a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics" title="Dark Horse Comics">Dark Horse Comics</a> in August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dota 2</i> has also been used in <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a> experiments, with the American <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> research company <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a> curating a system, known as the <a href="/wiki/OpenAI_Five" title="OpenAI Five">OpenAI Five</a>, that allows <a href="/wiki/Video_game_bot" title="Video game bot">bots</a> to learn how to play the game at a high skill level entirely through trail-and-error algorithms. The bots learn over time by playing against itself hundreds a times a day for months in a system that OpenAI calls "reinforcement learning", in which they are rewarded for actions such as killing an enemy and destroying towers.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Demonstrations of the bots playing against professional players have occurred at a number of events, such as <a href="/wiki/Dendi_(video_game_player)" title="Dendi (video game player)">Dendi</a>, a professional Ukrainian player of the game, losing to one of them in a live <a href="/wiki/1v1" class="mw-redirect" title="1v1">1v1</a> matchup at <a href="/wiki/The_International_2017" title="The International 2017">The International 2017</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> A year later, the ability of the bots had increased to work together as a full team of five, known as the <a href="/wiki/OpenAI_Five" title="OpenAI Five">OpenAI Five</a>, who then played and won against a team of semi-professional players in a demonstration game in August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after, OpenAI Five then played two live games against more skilled players at <a href="/wiki/The_International_2018" title="The International 2018">The International 2018</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> Although the bots lost both games, OpenAI considered it a successful venture, stating that playing against some of the best players in <i>Dota 2</i> allowed them to analyze and adjust their algorithms for future games.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<li id="cite_note-Polygon_guide-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polygon_guide_5-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Gies, Arthur. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.polygon.com/2017/8/2/16073588/the-normal-persons-guide-to-watching-competitive-dota-2-2017-edition">"The Normal Person's Guide to Watching Competitive Dota 2 (2017 Edition)"</a>. <i>Polygon</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170803171002/https://www.polygon.com/2017/8/2/16073588/the-normal-persons-guide-to-watching-competitive-dota-2-2017-edition">Archived</a> from the original on August 3, 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">.
